- Use `github.com/sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# OpenJDK Security Provider Registration Framework

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in openjdk/jdk that implement the security provider registration framework. Identify: the base Provider class with putService() (java.security.Provider), the SunJCE provider that registers crypto algorithms, the SunJSSE provider for SSL/TLS factories, the SunEC provider for elliptic curve algorithms, the Sun provider for core algorithms, and the ProviderConfig lazy-loading mechanism that maps provider names to classes.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/jdk--742e735d.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` (openjdk/jdk)

53-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the Java source files implementing the OpenJDK security provider registration framework. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

### **Core Framework Files:**
1. **Provider.java** - Base abstract class with the `putService()` method (line 1221) that providers use to register services
2. **ProviderConfig.java** - The lazy-loading mechanism mapping provider names to classes via a switch statement (lines 168-215)

### **Provider Implementations:**
3. **Sun.java** - Core provider for DSA, SHA digests, SecureRandom, X.509, keystores
4. **SunRsaSign.java** - RSA key operations and signatures
5. **SunJCE.java** - Cryptographic algorithms (AES, DES, ChaCha20, HMAC, key agreement, PBE)
6. **SunJSSE.java** - SSL/TLS support (KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext)
7. **SunEC.java** - Elliptic curve algorithms (ECDH, ECDSA, XDH, EdDSA)

### **Supporting Infrastructure:**
8. **SunEntries.java** - Service definitions for the Sun provider
9. **ProviderList.java** - Manages the ordered list of providers with semi-eager loading

The lazy-loading mechanism in **ProviderConfig.getProvider()** (lines 168-215) implements a switch statement that maps provider names directly to their concrete classes, enabling on-demand instantiation while caching loaded providers. This design improves JVM startup time by only loading providers when needed.

The answer file has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the framework.

Works with ProviderConfig to implement semi-eager loading, where providers are loaded only when actually needed. The ProviderList handles adding/removing providers, converting configurations to loaded providers, and managing provider preference order.\\n\\n**Service Registration Flow:**\\nEach provider's constructor calls putService() for each cryptographic service it provides. The putService() method (Provider.java:1221) registers the Service in an internal serviceMap indexed by type and algorithm name, and also stores property strings for compatibility. Providers can also define custom Service subclasses (like SunEC's ProviderService) to override the newInstance() method for dynamic instantiation logic.\\n\\n**Lazy Loading Flow:**\\nWhen Security.getProvider(name) is called, it triggers ProviderConfig.getProvider(), which either returns a cached Provider instance or instantiates the provider for the first time using the switch-based mapping. The Provider class also defines the inner Service class that encapsulates information about individual services (Signature, Cipher, KeyFactory, etc.).\\n\\n2. **ProviderConfig Lazy-Loading Mechanism** (sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): This is the central lazy-loading mechanism that maps provider names to their concrete classes. The `getProvider()` method (lines 152-219) uses a switch statement (lines 168-215) to handle provider instantiation. For core providers, it directly instantiates them:\\n   - \\\"SUN\\\" \u2192 sun.security.provider.Sun\\n   - \\\"SunRsaSign\\\" \u2192 sun.security.rsa.SunRsaSign\\n   - \\\"SunJCE\\\" \u2192 com.sun.crypto.provider.SunJCE\\n   - \\\"SunJSSE\\\" \u2192 sun.security.ssl.SunJSSE\\n   - \\\"SunEC\\\" \u2192 sun.security.ec.SunEC\\n   - \\\"Apple\\\" \u2192 apple.security.AppleProvider (via reflection for platform compatibility)\\n\\nFor other providers, it uses ServiceLoader and legacy reflection-based loading. The ProviderConfig also tracks loading state to prevent recursion and implements caching with volatile Provider field.\\n\\n**Provider Implementations:**\\n\\n3. **Sun Provider** (sun/security/provider/Sun.java): Implements core algorithms including DSA key generation, DSA signing, SHA-1/MD5/SHA-2/SHA-3 digests, SecureRandom, X.509 certificate handling, and keystore support (PKCS12, JKS, DKS). Services are defined in SunEntries class.\\n\\n4. **SunRsaSign Provider** (sun/security/rsa/SunRsaSign.java): Provides RSA key factory, keypair generation, and RSA signature algorithms. Services are populated from SunRsaSignEntries iterator.\\n\\n5. **SunJCE Provider** (com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java): The Java Cryptography Extension provider implementing symmetric ciphers (RSA, DES, Triple DES, AES, Blowfish, RC2, ARCFOUR, ChaCha20), cipher modes (ECB, CBC, CFB, OFB, PCBC, CTR, CTS, GCM), password-based encryption, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC algorithms, JCEKS keystore, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Services are registered via helper methods ps() and psA().\\n\\n6. **SunJSSE Provider** (sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): Implements SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory (SunX509, NewSunX509/PKIX), TrustManagerFactory (SunX509, PKIX variants), SSLContext factories for TLSv1/1.1/1.2/1.3, DTLSv1.0/1.2, and PKCS12 KeyStore support. Uses ps() helper method for registration.\\n\\n7. **SunEC Provider** (sun/security/ec/SunEC.java): Provides elliptic curve algorithms including EC KeyFactory, KeyPairGenerator, KeyAgreement (ECDH), signature schemes (SHA-*withECDSA, SHA3-*withECDSA with P1363 format variants), XDH key operations (X25519, X448), and EdDSA signature schemes (Ed25519, Ed448). Uses custom ProviderService and ProviderServiceA inner classes that extend Provider.Service.\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure:**\\n\\n8. **SunEntries** (sun/security/provider/SunEntries.java): Defines the set of Service objects for the Sun provider, including digest algorithms, signatures, key factories, keystores, certificate-related services, and secure random implementations.\\n\\n9. **ProviderList** (sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages the ordered list of providers configured via java.security file. Works with ProviderConfig to implement semi-eager loading, where providers are loaded only when actually needed. The ProviderList handles adding/removing providers, converting configurations to loaded providers, and managing provider preference order.\\n\\n**Service Registration Flow:**\\nEach provider's constructor calls putService() for each cryptographic service it provides. The putService() method (Provider.java:1221) registers the Service in an internal serviceMap indexed by type and algorithm name, and also stores property strings for compatibility. Providers can also define custom Service subclasses (like SunEC's ProviderService) to override the newInstance() method for dynamic instantiation logic.\\n\\n**Lazy Loading Flow:**\\nWhen Security.getProvider(name) is called, it triggers ProviderConfig.getProvider(), which either returns a cached Provider instance or instantiates the provider for the first time using the switch-based mapping. This lazy approach improves JVM startup time by only loading providers that are actually used.\"\n}\n",
